		<score>0.8</score>
		<shortDescription>Interesting character study</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Ang Lee's The Ice Storm starts off with Tobey Maguire talking of the paradox within The Fantastic Four comic books. This sets us up for the film, which is a paradox in itself. The paradox shows us how actions within a family unit can lead to a storm. This is epitomised materially by an actual storm that hits the neighbourhood, and has an effect on all of the characters. The start of the film is also ironic as both the director and the actor playing the character that reads the comic book would have their future in comic books; Ang Lee for 'The Hulk', and Tobey Maguire for the fabulous 'Spider-Man' films.The story takes place in a small neighbourhood in 1970's America and features two upper class families at it's centre; the Hood family, which consists of two parents (Kevin Kline and Joan Allen) and two children; a fourteen year old girl (Christina Ricci) and a sixteen year old boy (Tobey Maguire) and the Carver family, which consists of two parents (Sigourney Weaver and Jamey Sheridan) and two boys (Elijah Wood and Adam Hann-Byrd). It is mainly through the interactions between these families that the story progresses; Kevin Kline is having a purely sexual affair with Sigourney Weaver, which leads to suspicion and later jealousy from Joan Allen. At the same time, Christina Ricci is 'experimenting' with Elijah Wood and later his younger brother, which leads to protectiveness from her father etc. From this tight bond between the eight central characters, we are able to see why the characters do certain things, we see that it is their insecurities that drive them, usually to hypocrisy and it is this character study that makes The Ice Storm a good film. Due to the number of characters, and the relatively short running time of the film, it is impossible for them all to develop fully and for us to get to know all of them, and because of the way the relationships are shown, it makes the film seem deeper and more complex than it actually is. Two years later, a similar format to the one seen in this movie would be used to a much better effect; in a film called American Beauty. This predecessor never reaches the highs of that film.Ang Lee has assembled himself a marvellous here. Kevin Kline is an underrated actor who always gives a good performance, as he does here. Sigourney Weaver is ultra-seductive mode, and this is probably the sexiest she's ever been in a movie. Joan Allen is sultry as Kline's wife, but her performance is believable and she brings a great life to the movie. Meanwhile, on the younger side of the cast, Christina Ricci impresses very much as the smart and curious young lady of the film. She's a beautiful actress, and one with talent too. Her performance is the standout of the film for me; she's the most real and the most enticing by far. Despite being a big fan of Spider-Man, I've always found Tobey Maguire to be annoying. He's annoying here too; he has talent, but he's very annoying. Elijah Wood is as turgid as ever in this film. He would, of course, go on to become a 'big thing', but it's clear to see that he's rubbish, from this film and his later performances. As he would later show with Crouching Tiger, Hidden Dragon; Ang Lee has a great directorial flair, and he shows it off here. The film is also supremely well written and there isn't a line that appears out of place for the character that speaks it. This allows us to get to know the characters and that is what you need to do in a film of this ilk. The Ice Storm is overall a good film.</fullReview>
	</review>

Weaver's bored housewife is perhaps the ultimate ice-queen, but those around her are just as unworthy of any respect as she. Sure, the performances are great, particularly Kevin Kline's, but without any sympathy for its characters this film becomes a sterile and bleak experience. Watch this by all means, it is a well crafted film, but its subject and characterisations are as cold and unfulfilling as the titular ice storm.</fullReview>

		<score>0.1</score>
		<shortDescription>Beautiful but pointless</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Ang Lee's underplayed style and attention to detail are simply breathtaking. However, despite this being a story well told, it's just not worth the telling.The biggest failing is that the characters are underdrawn and uninvolving. They're so angst ridden and generally miserable that I just can't bring myself to care about what happens to any of them. This is in contrast to other Ang Lee films: Sense and Sensibility (lots of dialogue), Eat Drink Man Woman (exquisitly expressive acting), and Crouching Tiger, Hidden Dragon (sympathetic stereotypes that don't need a lot of dialogue to explain).Also, Kevin Kline is badly out of place, in stark contrast to the otherwise splendid cast. He is an enjoyable actor in fluff or stagey pieces, but is far too hammy to (under)play serious drama. To be fair, he helps to prevent the film from becoming too maudlin too quickly, but he seems unable to lay his upstaging instincts aside towards the end. More can often be less, Kevin.The same goes for the pointless voiceover by a character who isn't even central. This seems Bladerunner-like, and I can't help but wonder if it was tacked on afterwards. The music also strays a little towards the orchestral once or twice, rather than the sparse breaks that Ang Lee prefers. This spells post production nervousness, much as the casting of Kevin Kline might indicate the chill hand of commercialism forcing unfortunate compromises on a director who can demonstrably do better given decent material, talent and a free reign.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Another interesting mood piece from Ang Lee...</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>The icy atmosphere of THE ICE STORM is a metaphor for the icy relationships of two families living through the '70s in a middle class Connecticut neighborhood. Both families are rather dysfunctional with the adults and minors unable to establish a meaningful rapport.KEVIN KLINE and JANE ALLEN are particularly convincing as the parents whose marriage is definitely on shaky ground once he starts having an affair with a restless female neighbor (SIGOURNEY WEAVER), whose husband is away so often that his own kids don't even know when he's gone.Their son, TOBEY MAGUIRE, is the pivotal viewpoint for the youngsters, off to New York City to party with some friends but making the trip back to Connecticut at the height of the ice storm. All of the characters are similarly effected in some way by the storm, but unfortunately none of them really come as alive as the wintry landscapes. The cinematography is gorgeous, depicting the icicles glittering on branches and frozen patches of land.The production values are terrific, but the fault lies in the film's slow pacing and the lack of sufficient interest in the mostly unlikeable characters.Visually, it's a treat with some wonderful photography--but most of the characters are as cold and remote as the winter landscapes. It's not easy to care about any of them. Their emotional distance from each other is so apparent that it alienates the viewer from caring about them. But Kline and Allen do a terrific job as the parents most affected by the storm and its consequences.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Well-played but voyeuristic</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Is it well-acted? Yes. Is it well-played? Yes. Is it representative of real life? No. It is hollyweird's idea of what middle-class life is because they do not experience it. The movie is cynical and more like science-fiction than drama. But, it is engrossing and well-acted. Ang Lee is the king of depressing cynicism. The movie is highly voyeuristic and cannibalistic in its view of everyday life. But, I cannot fault the intention -- it accomplishes what it sets out to accomplish. So, in that context, it is excellently portrayed. However, only watch it if you have a fatalistic view of your neighbors. The comparisons to "American Beauty" have some credence but "Ice Storm" lacks a sense of humor about itself. This is a movie mistake -- wherein the director takes the material too seriously as if it were an ultimate truth. Good movie, bad taste in the mouth.</fullReview>

		<fullReview>The film, The Ice Storm, explores marital infidelity, adolescent irresponsibility and political changes with the Watergate incident, signifying not only is the climate changing outside but also in the wealthy suburbs of Connecticut and politically changing in the United States. 'The Ice Storm', takes place in 1973, in the New Canaan, Connecticut, as the storm is approaches within the city, several storms are taking place in the lives of the Hood and Carver family. Ben Hood is having an affair with his neighbor, Janey Carver. His wife Elena Hood is a shoplifter, who is being hit on by a longhaired minister, named Philip Edwards. The Hood kids Paul, Wendy, and Ben and Mikey Carver explore sex, drugs and other adolescent behaviors. The adults goes to a wife swapping party where men put their car keys in a bowl, and the women fish out a pair of keys and go home with the owners of the set. During the storm Mikey Carver decides to adventure outside without caution on to the slick and hazardous surface where dangerous power lines have fallen, causing an electrocution. Reality finally sinks in and the families realize their families are the most important in their life. The title 'Ice Storm' along with some other words in the movie had double meaning. For example, the storm represents the atmosphere of the climate, and it represented the storm in the family lives. The cracking of the trees was a metaphor of the cracking of the family. When you choose to venture out into the ice storm you could fall from the slippery surface, and the people in the film who choose to venture out into irresponsible behavior fall in drugs, sex and even death. Although the ice storm looks beautiful, the surface areas become slick, tree limbs grow heavy and crack under pressure and fall on power lines causing destruction. Adults are cracking under social pressure by cheating on their spouses, drinking alcohol, and doing drugs causing break down and destruction in the family, example spouse cheating, Janey Carver, ' Ben, you're boring me. I have a husband. I don't need for another one.' The parents do not really have an open line of communication with their kids. For example, Jim Carver: 'Hey guys, I'm back!' Mikey Carver, 'You were gone?' The kids are also into their own adolescent behaviors. Wendy Hood, 'I'll show you mine if you show me yours'. I did not like the movie, 'The Ice Storm'. My initial response was it was very weird and the ending was depressing. I found it strange for married couples to be wife swapping so openly. The parents were having affairs and spending very little time with their children. Wendy Hood tried to discuss the Watergate issue with her parents and they show very little interest in her conversation. The only fun the kids seem to be having was experimenting with sex and drugs. They all seem to hurt people they love and take for granted what is most important in their lives. The parents and the kids experimented with drugs, but for the 1970's, this seems to be politically accepted. The author made a great choice for the title of the film, 'The Ice Storm'. He really makes you think about your own life, your own choices and the consequences that may occur from your choices, when storms of life are raging.</fullReview>

		<fullReview>The movie takes place Thanksgiving 1973, in the small town of New Canaan, Connecticut. There are two families, the Cavers and the Hoods. At first glance the families are a stereotype of a suburban family living in an upper middle class neighborhood. There is nothing special or out of the ordinary about these families. The film just shows each individual's faults and how it affects the people that surround them. Initially, the movie seems boring. Being so accustomed to fast action movies, the slow pace this one take to develop leads you to believe nothing is really occurring between these two families. There is no hasty music or scenes; on the contraire it's slow and relaxing.At the surface, the father, Ben Hood, is a man of good hart, has difficulty expressing his real emotions and needs. During the whole film he tries to 'act' as a father, husband and neighbor. The mother, Elena, finds her self feeling empty seeking guidance in a 'Self Help Book' and questioning her spirituality. Her daughter, Wendy 14years of age, and son, Paul a 16 year old, try to commence their sexual life.Skin deep, things are very different. Families are becoming self destructive. Ben tries to drown his unhappiness with alcohol while he carries an unsatisfying affair with his neighbor's wife, Janey Caverns. Elena behaves as she knows nothing of the affair. She continues to act her role; simultaneously she grows bitter and angry. Wendy and Paul are caught in the middle of their parent's instability. Wendy expressed her discontent with the world by being verbal and rebellious, steeling, smoking, and exploring her sexuality with two brothers. Sam tries to find acceptance and heads to New York in search of a girl, socially and economically out is his reach.The night of the Ice Storm, everything changes in such a magnificent way. It begins with the scene were the Carvers son, Mickey, explains that when the temperature drops and it get cold, molecules don't move as much, making the 'air cleaner' as a simile . He suits up to explore the icy night and is sweep away in his exploration. As the storm develops, the air between each member is cleaned. By being forced to confront their inner feeling a spiritual freedom is found. Ben and Elena confront the affair and their unhappiness. The same nights Ben and Janey confront status of their affair and how unfulfilling it has become, putting an end to the relation. The same night Wendy loses her virginity with Sandy and the same night Sam confronts his feelings about sex with a woman learning how to deal with reject.All is clean again, but in order to appreciate all the thing that have occurred these families must experience real drama. That is when Ben Hoods discovers the lifeless body of Mikey on the street (he had been killed by an electrical line during his exploration). Ben takes the body to his parents house were every one, but Paul who is stuck on the train coming back from New York, is there. The shocking sight of a dead child brings everything into perspective. Latter, Paul's family arrives to the train station to pick him up. They are so relieved to see he is well, that Ben can not hold back his cry of sadness and happiness. This movie masterly represents the frigid emotional life of suburbia. The format of the movie, being slow and relaxing fools you to believe nothing is occurring. Just like these families who live their lives not appreciating the small things that surround them. By the time you become aware the movie is coming to an end, a shocking awakening of everything that had occurred hits you, making you rethink the whole film with greater appreciation while producing a fascinating emotional twist.</fullReview>

		<username>paul2001sw-1 (paul2001sw@yahoo.co.uk)</username>
		<score>0.5</score>
		<shortDescription>A quiet storm</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>There's a sadly fashionable tendency at the moment to dismiss films made in the 1970s as dated, often on no other grounds than their content, while fetishising modern movies that are set at that time. There's a certain arrogance in the viewpoint that people then did not know what was really important about their era, but that we do now; and regardless of which view history eventually confirms, it's hardly surprising that it is the supposedly dated originals that actually offer more demanding viewing than their contemporary competitors, wrapped in a comforting blanket of hindsight and nostalgia. In 'The Ice Storm', for example, we get a story of key parties, Action Men and Watergate; which, methinks, says more about us than it does about its characters.Ang Lee has proved an adept director in many genres, but aside from the predictably retro feel, 'The Ice Storm' has other limitations. Everyone (not just an exceeding young Christina Ricci) and everything looks beautiful: there's none of the authentic grime of a film by Mike Leigh or Ken Loach; while, closer to home it lacks the quirky vitality of Hal Hartley's early takes on American suburban life. There's also little in the way of conventional plot, just a lot of heavy symbolism and a hint of reassuring moralism at the end. Overall it's quite a cold film, perhaps because none of the characters are really held responsible for their actions; but it echoes with the empty seriousness of Oscar material. Not an awful film; but Lee has done better elsewhere.</fullReview>
	</review>

I would have liked to have seen more depth in the main characters, rather than having more and more players. I will not cite Ang Lee as being the cause of the failure to connect; he is a proven director. If the temperature is below two or three degrees Celsius, it may well snow, but it is impossible to rain, at least according to my old sciences school-book. At least this film convinces me far more than `American Beauty'. It has more interesting points to tell and the interpretations are far better, more real. 		<fullReview>CAUTION -- MIGHT CONTAIN A SPOILER OR TWO --The "Ice Storm" is set in 1973, in Connecticut, and the main protagonists are two families who live within walking distance, each with two teen-ish children. Kevin Cline and Joan Allen play one set, while Sigourney Weaver and Jamey Sheridan play the other parents. The children are played by Tobey Maguire, Elijah Woods, Christina Ricci, and a couple of others. I was a 20-something, married adult with children in the early 70s, and I certainly did NOT feel that this film represented that period very well, unless it was specific to New Canaan, in which case it did not have broad appeal anyway. The parents were entirely too permissive with their children. The film to me was too much of a dark caricature for me to enjoy it very much. So I give it a 6/10 rating, because it was well-filmed, and has an all-star cast. Other films which carry a theme of family dysfunctionality, which I think are better and which I rate higher are "The Nephew(98)", "My Life So Far(99), "The War(94)", "A Map of the World(99)", and "Eve's Bayou(97)", just to name a few. I can acknowledge that some viewers feel this is one of the best films they have seen, but for me it mostly falls flat, and my attitude at the end, after the boy is electrocuted and the father is bawling while the mother sleeps, "So what?"</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>A Major Disappointment</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>I rented "The Ice Storm" with very very high expectations. I had just seen "Crouching Tiger, Hidden Dragon", loved it, and wanted to see some more of Ang Lee's works. I had always had a lingering interest in the film after seeing Gene Siskel rank it #1 on his top 10 list for 1997. So I rented it, watched it, and am experiencing a feeling of disappointment no other film has ever matched. To be honest, I didn't like this film at all. Yes, it was well-made; yes, it had a very talented cast who all seemed to pull off their roles competently; yes, Ang Lee did a fine directing job. However, something is definitely missing from this film. It doesn't seem like it was made for any reason other than to show a pretty accurate family caricature that serves to inspire sympathy and intrigue. I only felt pity for the characters, which is different from sympathy, as it seemed like they had no redeeming qualities I could identify with. The film in general is very depressing, and the salvation it suggests the members of the two families achieve at the end of the film feels contrived and without substance. It strives to be an "Ordinary People" or "American Beauty", but it just doesn't work. I mean, it's like "American Beauty" but without any of the excitement, heart, or inspiration- it is lifeless. Any message sent in the story only serves to further the storyline and explain why some things are happening, and there is nothing positive that can be taken from this film. Perusing reviews, I see that a lot of people felt this film was excellent, of the highest quality. Yet, I also noticed that no reason was ever given in the reviews for why the reviewer thought the film was of such high merit. What really makes films great is the personal feelings they inspire, and the praise I saw was all objectively-based. There is no way this film can be enjoyed by any viewer while watching it. I think that people who would bother to see this film(pseudo-intellectuals like me) saw it, weren't sure what to think of it, and gave it a rating of 10 because Ang Lee directed it, it's not mainstream, and it's critical of the fragile family intrastructure. I'll have to give this a rating of 6, despite my feelings about it. It gets as high as a 6 because the performances were good and there were some great camera shots. Plus it is important that films like this exist, despite my misgivings about it.</fullReview>

So many times I was left wondering if that was all that was going to be said knowing full well in real life it never would have been left the way was in this film. And then further more, would you, as the one who committed the offense spend a good portion of the party with the woman that you were sleeping with knowing that your wife knew who she was? I wouldn't. And there are just too many false notes in the film like this one for me to believe that this film was as deep and chilling as people make it out to be. American Beauty is hands down a more intutitive film in exploring the problems with marriage, teens, sexual angst and a plethora of other issues that both movies seem to dive into.The Ice Storm is interesting and it is good in a few ways, but over all it falls short of my mild expectations.</fullReview>

		<username>bob the moo</username>
		<score>-1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>A classy and intriguing fable about the boredom of the middle-classes</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>In a small, comfortable suburb of Connecticut several families live their lives around one another as friends. Both the Hoods and Carvers are friends and have children who are also friends. Ben Hood is also having an affair with Janey Carver, while Jim is distant from his family. Elena Hood suspects but herself is trapped in a sort of frozen emotional reality. Meanwhile their children are experiencing the same sexual freedom in the air as their parents ? neither of which seem ready for it or able to deal with it.Ang Lee has made a name for himself on the bad of repressed emotions and restrained expression but this is easily one of his finest films as it portrays the inability of two family units to cope with the "sexual revolution" they experience in their own neighbourhood. The plot is not so much about one narrative flow but about the characters within the story ? making it perhaps harder to make it work, but yet Lee does it. Making it look easy, he steps into a culture and a time that he never experienced himself and made me feel like he must have first hand knowledge of the period ? which I suppose is due in a big way to Moody's novel and Schamus' screenplay. The sense of boredom is palatable and the sexual pleasure that is sought out as a result is well delivered as "innocent fun" that ultimately taints at best and destroys at worst. It is a strangely old-fashioned moral fable that is as compelling as it is low-key. I have read those who bemoan the film for its cold air and slow pace but I can only see the very things they take issue with as being reasons why the film is strong.The cast is classy and mostly spot-on, which is just what is needed with a film that is about characters more than a "this happened then this happened" narrative. Kline shows a real subtle touch that I have rarely seen from him and he is strong in one of the key roles. Weaver perhaps dominates Allen because her character is so much larger, but I found the latter to be much more rewarding in her performance. Just as impressive than the adults (if not more so) are the child actors. Maguire, Wood and Hann-Byrd are all excellent but Ricci just steals it as a girl discovering the power her sexuality and using it. Ironically the teenager who went onto greatest fame is Holmes, who is also the least of those here and the least worthy of her fame.Overall this is a classy and intriguing film that is professionally made and impressive. Some may struggle with the narrative but for most viewers the characters and themes will be more than enough to fill the film. Ang Lee does it again and the cast are more than able to take the material and produce the goods.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>All that acting out is gonna lead to trouble!</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Solemn movies which hope to expose the underside of human nature (like, say, "American Beauty") either intrigue audiences with their melancholy passages or simply put people off. Personal taste will have to determine where "The Ice Storm" falls. It certainly has a good cast of actors and an interesting production design. The picture had great possibilities, however both the central issue--how our carnal desires lead to trouble--and the answers we get are old news. There's the stifled housewife who dusts off an old bicycle so she can regain the freedom of her girlhood, the teenage daughter acting out what she doesn't see at home, the father having an affair with the neighbor. It plays out distressingly, like a familiar TV show. Although better than "American Beauty", "The Ice Storm", which takes place in 1973, makes obvious, rather redundant points against our culture (or, what was our culture), yet director Ang Lee is so overly-precise in his handling, he neglects to modulate the characters' behavior--and if this was intentional, he doesn't recognize the irony; he smooths over everything so all we have left to respond to are the performances. Christina Ricci and the ingratiating Tobey Maguire do the stand-out work; Kevin Kline, Sigourney Weaver and Joan Allen are reliable as always. **1/2 from ****</fullReview>

Even the way the writer has them respond to the weather, for God's sake!, is devoid of correct human observation. Having lived through some major ice storms in my life, I can tell you that no one goes walking, let alone driving, in such weather. If you can't get right so simple a thing as how people react to weather, then there is no hope whatsoever that anything else is right. This, and everything else in this movie, rings false, false, false. And don't tell me the performances were good because they were "nuanced." The actors were sleep-walking throughout, allowing vacancy to masquerade as heart-felt acting. Find a smile here--I dare you. No, the closest you will come to is a smirk--everyone is just too cynical, don't you know. Life is just so empty. Love doesn't really exist. No one has pets or hobbies or a past or emotions or passion. This is just the droppings of a writer whose only writing ability consists of spelling words correctly.Now, on the plus side, the photography of the ice storm is first rate. But that's akin to saying "Other than that, Mrs. Lincoln, how was the play?" There just isn't any point to this drivel. The nineties, mercifully, are over, and so are movies like Ice Storm and American Beauty. They are embarrassing reminders of the moral bankruptcy of that period's art.</fullReview>

		<date>2008-05-18</date>
		<username>Bill Slocum (bill.slocum@gmail.com)</username>
		<score>0.4</score>
		<shortDescription>Dysfunction Junction</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Suburban anomie turns deadly - deadly dull that is - in this adaptation of Rick Moody's tale of next-door neighbors discovering the jaws of life in 1970s New Canaan, Connecticut.There were three slice-of-life films set in the American 1970s made in the 1990s, split up chronologically and geographically as if by design. In reverse order, "Boogie Nights" covered the West Coast in the late '70s, "Dazed And Confused" central Texas in the mid-'70s, and this focused on the East Coast in 1973. "Ice Storm" aimed closest to where I lived, yet the film feels the furthest afield of any '70s I remember. There's no crunchy, funky, good-time neon-blue candy power-pop feeling coming off this baby. It's cold, emotionless, almost Scandinavian, and not in an ABBA-ish way.Thanksgiving, 1973. While the Watergate scandal consumes the country, the Hoods and Carvers hunker down for some holiday cheer, little imagining the storm brewing over their heads. When Ben Hood (Kevin Kline) and Janey Carver (Sigourney Weaver) aren't meeting for illicit sex, kids Mikey Carver (Elijah Wood) and Wendy Hood (Christina Ricci) do the same. Elena Hood (Joan Allen) alone seems to sense something seriously wrong, but is too locked into her own cocoon to do anything.The problem with "Ice Storm" isn't just that the plot, as it develops, feels a little too dire for the situation. The problem is it's hard to care. The characters aren't awful, not even Janey, despite Weaver's tarantula-lady wardrobe. They are simply inert and unsympathetic, living la vida coma with their prescription drugs and meaningless sex games.I want to totally align myself with Graham Deans Williamson's review from August 31, 2004: There's a lot of good things in this film that never come together, and not enough surface pleasure to make the medicine go down smoother.Director Ang Lee and screenwriter James Schamus make a point of hitting us over the head with the ice theme, it forever crackles in trays, rattles in glasses, and crunches beneath our feet. No metaphor is left unhammered, from the opening dissertation by older son Paul Hood (Tobey Maguire) regarding the comic-book heroes Fantastic Four as symbolic of family, "the closer you are drawn back in, the deeper into the void you go." When Wendy makes her move on Mikey, she wears a rubber Nixon mask, the ultimate symbol of corruption, although Lee and Schamus conversely take pains to present their pubescent explorations as the only thing about this life worth having.There are also the ridiculous contrivances, such as a "key party" where husbands and wives swap partners as if it is some casual New Canaan tradition, never mind the facts of how gossip about such a thing would have gone down the next day in the kind of uptight WASPy enclave we are presented with here. Much of the high drama at the movie's conclusion falls into this category as well."The Ice Storm" is the kind of film I wish I could like, having lived through the time period and remembering well the sense of society crumbling around me, along with the heady pleasure of unbridled kookiness. But if it had been in real life like it had been in the movie, I would have been better off kidnapped by the Symbionese Liberation Army. It's hard to care much when no one on screen does.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<shortDescription>One step above 'A complete waste of time'</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>This film has a great cast, a very skilled director and crew but it was all for nothing. Ang Lee has directed at least two very good films (Sense and Sensibility &amp; Ride with the Devil) and two over-rated films (this waste of film stock and Crouching Tiger).The story takes place in suburbia but not any suburbia that ever existed except in someone?s bad acid trip. The cinematography of this film by Frederick Elmes is fantastic as is the production design of Mark Friedberg it is just a shame that it was thrown away on such a bad script. Rating 2 stars out of 10.If you must see, a movie by Mr. Lee rent ?Ride with the Devil? where Mr. Maguire shows that he can act. If you want a movie with Mr. Kline rent, ?Life As A House?, Ms. Allen and Mr. Maguire are Oscar material in ?Pleasantville?, Mr. Wood was good in ?Lord of the Rings? and Ms. Holmes shines in ?Wonder Boys?.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>null</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Now, it's only been 12 hours since I screened "Ice Storm" and I gotta say the material falls surely into that slot in my brain reserved for material that is not disposable. "The Ice Storm" is soul source material that resonates in the long term, Cassavetes-style.The performances are A+, the art direction exemplary, the story a well -structured, multiply parallel progression presented with a high degree of tension generated by offscreen awareness of plot/character developments.This film IS pressure, temptation, collapse carefully dragging the viewer where you know you don't wanna go, but secretly can't help needing to find out the truth from the Truthteller, and you know you're gonna get the real magillah. Ugly, icky, and at times disturbingly stimulating (I shudder )."Ice" is like knowing there is going to be a serious accident on the highway at a particular road marker, you are compelled to go stand at the spot and watch it, then you can't turn away from the scene after the collision occurs.The only problem/issue that continues to come up in my analysis is the presence of the director's hand in all this. I am recognizing that what I think is missing or lacking is not a failure of the director, but is, rather a conditioned expectation of a non-descript cinematic element that I NEED to be represented. When something unique comes along with this level of cinematic skill and quality star value/performance, I apparently have this need to also feel an awareness of the filmmaker's consciousness in an overt sense."Ice" is NOT this. Ang transfixes the plot/story drama with covert control techniques that simultaneously disarm and dominate your conscious faculties , while skillfully cranking up the Emotionometer by creating a conscious, quasi-real time frame/spatial identity to this suburban nightmare. I have a deep respect for those special, few-and-far-between filmmakers reminding me that there is more than one way to direct a contemporary film.Beware, this is one that will stay with you for a long time...</fullReview>

		<date>2005-09-09</date>
		<username>Jackson Booth-Millard</username>
		<score>0.8</score>
		<shortDescription>The Ice Strom</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>From director Ang Lee (Crouching Tiger, Hidden Dragon, Brokeback Mountain), this is an entry in the book 1001 Movies You Must See Before You, I needed to see it again to see if I agree. Basically it is Thanksgiving 1973 in New Canaan, Conneticut, during the days when the Watergate scandal has unfolded with President Nixon as the most guilty involved. The story focuses on neighbouring families, the Hoods with husband/father Benjamin 'Ben' (Kevin Kline), wife/mother Elena (The Bourne Supremacy's Joan Allen), son Paul (Spider-Man's Tobey Maguire) and daughter Wendy (Sleepy Hollow's Christina Ricci), and the Carvers with mother Janey (BAFTA winning, and Golden Globe nominated Sigourney Weaver), husband/father Jim (Jamey Sheridan) and sons Mikey (Elijah Wood) and Sandy (Jumanji's Adam Hann-Byrd). The grown-ups are having troubles, Ben is drinking, in a dissatisfying marriage and having a not passionate affair with the bored Janey, Elena is also bored but unsure what to do about it, and Jim is hardly involved with his family. The youngsters are no different, Wendy is playing sexual games with a few boys from school and next door, Paul who sometimes uses drugs and compares life to the Fantastic Four comics is trying bed Libbets Casey (Katie Holmes), Sandy has a thing for Wendy, and Mikey has a thing for violence. The clear fact is that the two families lives all connect together in some way, and neither the parents or children of either clan communicate properly with each other. This may change when the cold weather comes along, and an ice storm forces the generations to face their problems head on. Elena does discover the affair between Ben and Janey, Wendy and Sandy do get close to each other, Paul looks forward to returning home after seeing Libbets, and tragedy strikes when Mikey is electrocuted resting on guardrail struck by a power line. In the end, the Hoods and Carvers have probably learnt some needed home truths with the devastating events adding to affect, but they try to pull together. Also starring Henry Czerny as George Clair. The casting of Kline goes against what you'd expect from him perfectly, Weaver and Allen I agree are the strong female characters, and the casting of young talents like Maguire, Wood, Ricci and even Hann-Byrd is fantastic. It is a good family based ensemble drama that really makes you feel something for each and every character, and the ice storm itself is well done as well, a very accomplished film that should certainly be seen. It was nominated the BAFTA for Best Adapted Screenplay. Sigourney Weaver was number 20 on The 100 Greatest Movie Stars. Very good!</fullReview>
	</review>
